
============== high level task decomposition ================
[{'objective': 'Rewrite the polynomial constraint in terms of symmetric sums or simpler expressions involving a, b, and c'}, {'objective': 'Use the sum constraint a + b + c = 300 to reduce the problem to an equation with fewer variables or symmetric functions'}, {'objective': 'Formulate and solve the resulting equation(s) to find all nonnegative integer triples (a, b, c) satisfying both constraints'}, {'objective': 'Count the number of valid triples (a, b, c) obtained from the solutions'}]
============== task analysis ================
1. Extract and Summarize Given Information:
- Variables: Nonnegative integers a, b, c.
- Constraints:
  - Linear: a + b + c = 300.
  - Nonlinear: a^2b + a^2c + b^2a + b^2c + c^2a + c^2b = 6,000,000.
- Objective: Find the number of triples (a,b,c) satisfying both conditions.

2. Analyze Relationships Between Components:
- The first equation restricts the sum of the variables to a fixed total.
- The second equation is symmetric in a, b, c and involves terms of the form a^2b and similar permutations, which can be rewritten or factored to reveal underlying structure.
- The nonlinear condition likely imposes a strong constraint on the distribution of values among a, b, and c.
- The symmetry suggests that permutations of a solution triple are also solutions, affecting counting.

3. Identify the Field of Study:
- Primary domain: Combinatorics and Number Theory (integer solutions to Diophantine equations).
- Secondary domain: Algebra (symmetric polynomials, polynomial identities).
- Context: Counting integer solutions under polynomial constraints, common in combinatorial number theory and mathematical competitions.

4. Highlight Aspects Needing Clarification:
- Whether permutations of (a,b,c) are considered distinct or identical solutions (likely distinct since triples are ordered).
- The complexity of the nonlinear equation suggests potential multiple solution sets or the need for factorization.
- Assumptions: Variables are nonnegative integers; no further constraints on ordering.
- Potential challenge: The nonlinear equation's form may require rewriting or bounding to find integer solutions efficiently.

Using the linear constraint a+b+c=300, we substitute b+c=300 - a, a+c=300 - b, and a+b=300 - c, resulting in 300(a^2 + b^2 + c^2) - (a^3 + b^3 + c^3). To express this in terms of elementary symmetric polynomials, recall the definitions: e1 = a + b + c = 300, e2 = ab + bc + ca, and e3 = abc. We use the identity a^3 + b^3 + c^3 = e1^3 - 3e1 e2 + 3e3. Also, a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = e1^2 - 2e2. Substituting these into the expression gives 300(e1^2 - 2e2) - [e1^3 - 3e1 e2 + 3e3] = 300*300^2 - 600 e2 - (300^3 - 900 e2 + 3 e3) = 27,000,000 - 600 e2 - 27,000,000 + 900 e2 - 3 e3 = 300 e2 - 3 e3. Hence, the nonlinear constraint simplifies to 300 e2 - 3 e3 = 6,000,000, or equivalently, 100 e2 - e3 = 2,000,000. The elementary symmetric polynomials for variables a, b, c are: σ1 = a + b + c, σ2 = ab + bc + ca, σ3 = abc. Given σ1 = 300, we can use known symmetric identities to express sums of powers.
